<div id="review_138117865" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138117865" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138117865?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8217236-the-yellow-wallpaper">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of stories with lots of subtext, classic horror readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=kindle-book">kindle-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=insane-or-mentally-ill-character">insane-or-mentally-ill-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=victorian">victorian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=tales-to-chill-your-blood">tales-to-chill-your-blood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=women-s-issues">women-s-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=unreliable-narrator">unreliable-narrator</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=gothic-fiction">gothic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2011-reading">2011-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=short-story-collection">short-story-collection</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138117865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16413917336473121917">This is my second read of this story, and I gave it four stars this time. It's a very well-written story. Ms. Gilmore crafted this tale in such a way that you feel as twisted as the narrator does. It's clear that mental illness plays a major role in the mindset of the narrator. But, there is a little shred of doubt (at least in my mind) that there might be some otherworldly component. It's hard to tell, because we are seeing things through her perceptions, which are clearly not rational.<br/><br/>I think </span>
  <span id="freeText16413917336473121917" style="display:none">This is my second read of this story, and I gave it four stars this time. It's a very well-written story. Ms. Gilmore crafted this tale in such a way that you feel as twisted as the narrator does. It's clear that mental illness plays a major role in the mindset of the narrator. But, there is a little shred of doubt (at least in my mind) that there might be some otherworldly component. It's hard to tell, because we are seeing things through her perceptions, which are clearly not rational.<br /><br />I think there is a powerful message here. Husbands often had way too much control over their wives. Probably still the case. The husband in this story treated his wife like she was a child. He dismissed her thoughts and needs, and constantly told her what was best for her. He didn't treat her like a partner. I think that his treatment of her played a role in her deterioration. <br /><br />I read about the author, Charlotte Perkins Gilman, on Wikipedia. She was a feminist who crusaded to help women in the time period in which she lived. I could see how she masterfully threaded some real-life themes into this story. It would give any reader something to think about, and I imagine it made a few people, particularly men, angry at the time in which it was published.<br /><br />This is considered a feminist work. I don't think that you have to be a feminist to appreciate this message. As an egalitarian, I definitely felt this message. I felt sympathy for this woman. I think that she felt caged in and didn't have her needs met, and something inside of her twisted until she left sanity behind. It's quite a sad thing that the people who loved her contributed by their gentle neglect. If she had been listened to, and really heard, maybe things would have gone differently. <br /><br />This is just my perception of this story. No doubt, a different reader will glean a dissimilar meaning from this work. In my opinion, The Yellow Wallpaper is a story that should be read more than one time. I feel I encountered more subtext and layers upon the second read. I'll keep it on my Kindle, because it's one I would like to revisit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16413917336473121917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3232866677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15391200712817236790">In my 9th grade English class we watched the movie of this short story in class, but we never read it. It has been on my list to read for years. I was intrigued by the movie and thought it was interesting. When I found how it was a short story, I decided it was time to read this.<br/><br/>I haven’t read Charlotte’s work before and she has beautiful prose. For a short story, it’s very powerful. This wall paper and how it comes to dominate her thoughts are amazing. This woman is depressed and her husband re</span>
  <span id="freeText15391200712817236790" style="display:none">In my 9th grade English class we watched the movie of this short story in class, but we never read it. It has been on my list to read for years. I was intrigued by the movie and thought it was interesting. When I found how it was a short story, I decided it was time to read this.<br /><br />I haven’t read Charlotte’s work before and she has beautiful prose. For a short story, it’s very powerful. This wall paper and how it comes to dominate her thoughts are amazing. This woman is depressed and her husband rents a house for the summer and sticks her up in a room alone with yellow wallpaper. She keeps asking to be around people and society, but he thinks he knows best, being a physician. The isolation is the worst thing for this woman.<br /><br />I love the use of wallpaper in this story. It is well done. How she begins to see things in the wallpaper gradually illustrated the madness she is dealing with. I could see this idea as a Stephen King story that uses this devise, but it is actually some ghoul in the wallpaper being freed for real. <br /><br />It’s a story of someone asking about what she needs and the people who love her don’t listen and think they know best. <br /><br />I highly recommend this story. It’s a fast read and interesting. I’m glad I got around to reading.</span>

<div id="review_1789153496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1789153496" />
    <a title="Rae Meadows" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3184-rae-meadows"><img alt="Rae Meadows" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455814351p2/3184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1789153496?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rae Meadows" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rae Meadows" href="/user/show/3184-rae-meadows">Rae Meadows</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1789153496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5833917559025752054">I'm not sure I have much to add about this story from 1892, but I had never read it and was glad to finally do so. It is an incredibly sad story of a woman's descent into mental illness hastened by a rest cure imposed by her physician husband. There are different layers, one being an early feminist critique of women's subjectivity in a marriage, through the story of a woman whose agency has been taken away by her husband. There are a couple of eerie mentions of a baby in another room taken care </span>
  <span id="freeText5833917559025752054" style="display:none">I'm not sure I have much to add about this story from 1892, but I had never read it and was glad to finally do so. It is an incredibly sad story of a woman's descent into mental illness hastened by a rest cure imposed by her physician husband. There are different layers, one being an early feminist critique of women's subjectivity in a marriage, through the story of a woman whose agency has been taken away by her husband. There are a couple of eerie mentions of a baby in another room taken care of by someone else (her child though she doesn't say it), which might signal postpartum depression. <br /><br />The woman narrating the story in a secret journal has a breathless, flightiness to her voice which seems all the sadder as she is consumed by the yellow wallpaper in her room, by the life she imagines the patterns have taken on. She becomes both more languid in her dealings with her husband and more manic in her journal, her voice infused with a shrill, unnerving energy. She sees women creeping about behind the wallpaper until she has pulled it all off and creeps around her room, having lost the tether to reality. It's a short and worthwhile read, as is Gilman's biography included. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5833917559025752054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12203079494069084227">The final five minutes of this audiobook, I went “yeah that sounds about right”. And I meant that in a non sarcastic way possible. <br/><br/>This is probably the most believable gothic story I have read. That is also a sincere opinion. <br/><br/>Just that it was such a trippy ride and only the matter of time as to when she would snap and when she did, it was just the most natural thing in the world at that point. <br/><br/><br/><br/>Listened @ Horrorbabble</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1561587596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10695981612755402606">Wow, this is a powerful short-story that makes quite a statement about insanity, the need of a woman to have choices and independence, and the unintentional cruelties of those who fail to listen or acknowledge another's suffering. I was stunned by how much Gilman managed to say in so few pages. <br/><br/></span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText1949906321860085012" style="display:none">This book stands out in my mind mainly because of an argument I had with our English teacher that lasted the length of an entire English class, over whether or not the room was actually originally a childrens' playroom, or some kind of sinister crazy-wife-locking-up-room.<br /><br />My argument: "She's an unreliable narrator!     <span class="greyText">Recommended to Bonnie by: </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227084672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11355952822825334836"><i>’This paper looks to me as if it KNEW what a vicious influence it had! <br/><br/>There is a recurrent spot where the pattern lolls like a broken neck and two bulbous eyes stare at you upside down. I get positively angry with the impertinence of it and the everlastingness. Up and down and sideways they crawl, and those absurd, unblinking eyes are everywhere. There is one place where two breadths didn't match, and the eyes go all up and down the line, one a little higher than the other.’</i><br/><br/>Man, that yellow wal</span>
  <span id="freeText11355952822825334836" style="display:none"><i>’This paper looks to me as if it KNEW what a vicious influence it had! <br><br>There is a recurrent spot where the pattern lolls like a broken neck and two bulbous eyes stare at you upside down. I get positively angry with the impertinence of it and the everlastingness. Up and down and sideways they crawl, and those absurd, unblinking eyes are everywhere. There is one place where two breadths didn't match, and the eyes go all up and down the line, one a little higher than the other.’</i><br><br>Man, that yellow wallpaper has some nerve. Sure, the woman was obviously going insane prior to moving to this house with that vicious yellow wallpaper but honestly? If that worthless husband of hers would have just changed it when she told him to none of this would have happened. So I blame the husband. And that vicious yellow wallpaper. <br><br>But honestly?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361838i/712888.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If that shit was on my walls I’d probably go crazy too.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2n1Suhh9fnZEP2k18XM+hgXzZkWsSGY78mMJg9lPcln0h9VxpcuxNzM98iTzv1j85tjnToXBMTn3LvAnTyo+Fg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1bu2iCm5YTBvg6NY6e6CEVsEGKJRlLjXcBlIKyHBuvv7QTFDlA+ucRiBOEnrIuRruC+ZqXgd79V1VLGPt6T2tA==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_75090'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/75090.A_Good_Man_Is_Hard_To_Find?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">A Good Man Is Hard To Find<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/22694.Flannery_O_Connor?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Flannery O\'Connor<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.92 avg rating &mdash; 6,649 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1949\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer8845114678897505723\">A Good Man Is Hard to Find is Flannery O\'Connor\'s most famous and most discussed story. O\'Connor herself singled it out by making it the title piece of her first collection and the story she most often chose for readings or talks to students. It is a<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText8845114678897505723\" style=\"display:none\">A Good Man Is Hard to Find is Flannery O\'Connor\'s most famous and most discussed story. O\'Connor herself singled it out by making it the title piece of her first collection and the story she most often chose for readings or talks to students. It is an unforgettable tale, both riveting and comic, of the confrontation of a family with violence and sudden death. More than anything else O\'Connor ever wrote, this story mixes the comedy, violence, and religious concerns that characterize her fiction.\n\nThis casebook for the story includes an introduction by the editor, a chronology of the author\'s life, the authoritative text of the story itself, comments and letters by O\'Connor about the story, critical essays, and a bibliography. The critical essays span more than twenty years of commentary and suggest several approaches to the story--formalistic, thematic, deconstructionist-- all within the grasp of the undergraduate, while the introduction also points interested students toward still other resources. Useful for both beginning and advanced students, this casebook provides an in-depth introduction to one of America\'s most gifted modern writers.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"8845114678897505723\" By putting African American women\'s voices at the center of the narrative for the first time, &quot;Everyday Use&quot; anticipated the focus of an entire generation of black women writers. This casebook includes an introduction by the editor, a chronology of Walker\'s life, an authoritative text of &quot;Everyday Use&quot; and of &quot;In Search of Our Mothers\' Gardens,&quot; an interview with Walker, six critical essays, and a bibliography.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/29527.Charlotte_Perkins_Gilman">About Charlotte Perkins Gilman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/29527.Charlotte_Perkins_Gilman"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1238281005p3/29527.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/29527.Charlotte_Perkins_Gilman">Charlotte Perkins Gilman
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
937
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11111966466268308163">Charlotte Perkins Gilman, also known as Charlotte Perkins Stetson, was a prominent American sociologist, novelist, writer of short stories, poetry, and nonfiction, and a lecturer for social reform. She was a utopian feminist during a time when her accomplishments were exceptional for women, and she served as a role model for future generations of feminists because of her unorthodox concepts and li</span>
  <span id="freeText11111966466268308163" style="display:none">Charlotte Perkins Gilman, also known as Charlotte Perkins Stetson, was a prominent American sociologist, novelist, writer of short stories, poetry, and nonfiction, and a lecturer for social reform. She was a utopian feminist during a time when her accomplishments were exceptional for women, and she served as a role model for future generations of feminists because of her unorthodox concepts and lifestyle. Her best remembered work today is her semi-autobiographical short story, "The Yellow Wallpaper", which she wrote after a severe bout of post-partum depression.<br /><br />She was the daughter of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1797234.Frederic_B__Perkins" title="Frederic B. Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Frederic B. Perkins</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11111966466268308163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
